font-size: 12pt;\">Zinc silicate is an inorganic paint. This automatically means it is insoluble in organic solvents . It is durable, heat resistant and abrasion resistant. It&nbsp; has outstanding mechanical strength and provides galvanic protection. <b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><o:p></o:p></b></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">The coating thickness is 80 microns--- single airless spray coat on a good gritblasted surface. &nbsp;As long as the zinc and iron are in contact, atmospheric oxidation spares the iron and effects the zinc. Thick paint spray will crack especially if not continiously stirred.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Cargoes tend to be aDsorbed rather than aBsorbed. It has no reaction with solvent/water mixtures. Dedicated methanol carriers are zinc silicate coated. They can be loaded with methanol again and again without ventilation. Venting is no so crucial as for epoxy tanks whose coatings softens. However it is better if tanks are ventilated. As sometimes wall waSh will show HC/color. Vent for 1 or 2 days to eliminate this problem. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Zinc Silicate salts are produced throughout the active life of the coating which appear as white patches. This is normal and will not cause a problem uless it is extracted by a wall wash surveyor. Even if these white salts are removed they will be regenerated over a period of time. Small damages to coating are self healing by electrochemical reaction.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Since the coating cannot handle pH values between 9 and 14 , remember LAC and caustic are extremely harmful. So in zinc tanks use 0.05% Teepol/ Genepol. Special acid cleaners like bufferclean 5.5 ( citric acid of pH 5.5 )can be used. Bufferclean 5.5 removes all zinc white salts and brings it down like snow fall.&nbsp; Buffer solution resists any change of its pH value due to dilution or an addition of solution of acid/ alkali. The process by which H+ or OH- ions are removed so that pH remains constant is known as buffer action.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Please remember dried detergent can also cause white patches. For tankcleaning 80 deg C water temp can be used. Zinc can tolerate higher temperatures than epoxy.&nbsp; However due to its porosity zinc tanks should first be cleaned at moderate temp and then only cleaning temp can be increased. Tallow/ animal fat when heated increases in acidity near heating coils. Also esters , alcohols, amines, chlorinated and brominated compounds should not have moisture content greater than 0.01% ( 100 ppm ). Molasses when diluted especially by bad quality fresh water from lakes etc create acids within 24 hours which attack coating. Continious exposure to salt/ FW reduces life of coating. Toluene and Xylene are good degreasers. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Zinc paint is <i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\">resistant </i>to : Phenols and cresols, aromatic hydrocarbons BTX, alcohols and ketones, CTC, EDC, Trichloroethylene, and esters like amyl and ethyl acetate provided tank surfaces are free of moisture. Resistant to Acetone, Acrylonitrile, Ethanol, Methanol, IPA, MEK, Methyl Acrylate, VAM, Butyl acetate, Ekta Solve, Adiponitrile etc. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Zinc paint is <i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\">not resistant to</i>:&nbsp; Acetic acid, Alkaline Glycol Monoalkyl Ether, Diethanolamine, Diethyl Suphate, Brake fluid, Vinyl Acetate, Pentanoic acid, Triethanolamine, Nonyl Phenol, Ethyenediamine, Ethyl Hexanoic acid, Polyethylene Polyamine, Ethatholamine, Aviation turbine fuel, &nbsp;alkalies greater than pH 9, acids less than pH 6.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 12.9pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-line-height-rule: exactly; mso-pagination: none; tab-stops: 34.0pt; text-autospace: none;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Fatty acids of veg/ animal oils attack zinc silicate paint which can cause zinc to shed contaminating cargo. Amines water content if &gt;500 ppm ( 0.05%) can cause alkali attack. So to prevent water contamination tank must be dry and nitrogen blanketed. Never use hot water for precleaning veg/ animal oils in zinc tanks because they have FFA (free fatty acids ). The manufacturers of zinc silicate coating describe a max FFA content of 2.5 as the limit. In practice this limit is way too high. </span><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Zinc-silicate-coatedtanks<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.15pt;\"> </span>are<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.3pt;\"> </span>not<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.2pt;\"> </span>us<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">e</span>d<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\"> </span>for<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.2pt;\"> </span>crude<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\"> e</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.05pt;\">d</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">i</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.05pt;\">b</span>le<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\"> </span>fats<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.25pt;\"> </span>a<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">n</span>d<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.25pt;\"> </span>oils,<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.15pt;\"> </span>un<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">le</span>ss the<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.2pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">a</span>cid<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.15pt;\"> </span>value<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\"> </span>is<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.35pt;\"> </span>1<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.4pt;\"> </span>or <span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.05pt;\">u</span>nder<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.6pt;\"> .</span><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Recirc of veg/ animal oil in coated tank is a must to prevent sedimentation and also to equalize the FFA content between the upper and lower layers. Since zinc lining is porous prolonged pre cleaning with ambient water is advisable after drying oils before introducing chemicals. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><i><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">FFA</span></i><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"> content may increase rapidly when cleaning is prematurely stopped. Semi-drying vegetable and animal oils react with oxygen to form a varnish like polymeric layer which is very difficult to remove. If there is delay in washing drying oils to prevent the oxidized varnish from forming on the bulkheads the air should be removed the empty tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp4\" style=\"line-height: normal; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">If a zinc silicate tank has been attacked you can see a thin layer of white dust on the surface OR the coating gives a porous appearance. White salts caused due to alkali PH&gt;9 attack are insoluble calcium and magnesium salts. Only bufferclean 5.5 can remove such white salts and the tank gets a fresh appearance. Never allow salt to dry on the coating after sea water wash. Salt electrolyte makes the coating sacrificial.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Zinc silicate tanks are not considered suitable for continious immersion in water. The surface is porous and cargo invades into pores and capillaries. Cleaning is similar to regeneration of an aDsorber bed. This is done by heating to greater than BP. Unlike epoxy de aDsorbsion occurs quite fast. Methanol removes non volatile matter from the pores/ capillaries. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Sometimes certain polymerizing cargoes are inhibited by ammonia derived stabilizers. Pl ensure that this cargo is not stowed in zinc silicate tanks---lest you get a polymerized tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">It is usual for MEG FG shippers to state in writing that zinc tanks are not suitable. There is no harm if you are able to pass the wall wash and the first foot. The discharge port samples will be good enough.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Zinc painting or touching is not usually done at sea as sea is not a perfect place. However I do remember 100% gritblasting ( 140 tons of grit to SA2.5 )and zinc silicate airless spray painting 2 cargo tanks on a pacific voyage in perfect conditions using shipstaff round the clock. The Sigma Silgauard paint involved was a 2 component fresh water moisture curing zinc rich&nbsp; ethyl silicate coating. To achieve 80 microns 9 sq metre per litre paint is required.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;Binder to zinc powder ratio is 3 :1.&nbsp; Zinc powder is added to the binder ( never vice versa )while continiously mechanically agitating using a pneumatic stirrer. Then strain the mixture through a 40 mesh screen just in case some lumps are present. The paint must be agitated continiously during the application. If the application temp is greater than 30 deg use 10% by volume of thinner. Potlife&nbsp; 20 deg c is just 6 hours ---so do not mix in large quantities. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"><br />\n</span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><a href=\"http://www.blogger.com/post-edit.g?blogID=3564735312144269387&amp;postID=7337010388864577263\" name=\"zinc\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">The high levels&nbsp;of zinc dust giving zinc-zinc metal contact resulting in cathodic protection similar to those obtained from galvanising. <o:p></o:p></span></a></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><a href=\"http://www.blogger.com/post-edit.g?blogID=3564735312144269387&amp;postID=7337010388864577263\" </span>prevail.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 12.0pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .5in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 1.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-line-height-rule: exactly; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 12.9pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-line-height-rule: exactly; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">The<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.45pt;\"> </span>re<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">m</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.05pt;\">o</span>val<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.25pt;\"> </span>of<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.55pt;\"> </span>volati<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">l</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.25pt;\"> </span>liqu<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">i</span>ds<span style=\"letter-spacing: after next cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Only zinc safe chemicals can be used for tankcleaning <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow; color: red; font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">REMEMBER-- A &nbsp;\"ZINC SAFE TANK\" &nbsp;CLEANING CHEMICAL IS NOTHING BUT A LIQUID WITH A pH OF WITHIN THE RANGE 5.5 TO 9.5 -- &nbsp;ANYTHING BEYOND THIS RANGE AND YOU CAN KISS THE COATING GOODBYE. &nbsp;</span></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: blue;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;\">Once i had taken over a zinc silicate coated chemical tanker-- the muffs had destroyed all the coating. When you use DI water or DEMI water generators with two cylinders ( not MIXED bed ) you should know what you are doing. &nbsp;If the acidic output pH is less than 6 , the coating gets permanently damaged.</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<br />\n<div style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;\"><span class=\"apple-converted-space\"><span style=\"color: black;\">F</span></span><span style=\"color: black;\">iltered water is first passed through cation exchange cylinder which removes CA2+/ MG2+ ( water hardness ions ) cations from it and an equivalent amount of H+ ions are released into the water. The water is now softened. &nbsp;(THIS ACIDIC WATER CAN DESTROY YOUR ZINC SILICATE COATING WHICH CANNOT TAKE pH LESS THAN 6.)<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;\">Then this water is passed through an anion exchange cylinder which removes SO42- CL- ( chlorides ) anions from it and an equivalent amount of OH- ions are released into the water. The chlorides are now removed. The water is now called de ionized water or de mineralized water.</span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: blue; font-size: medium;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><br />\n<br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"><o:p>&nbsp;CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL ( 28 YEARS IN COMMAND )</o:p></span></div><br />\n<div><br />\n</div><div><br />\n</div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TAXsGRbPSsI/AAAAAAAAAdI/0YFnEeHxhVE/s320/e2.jpg\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">EPOXY TANK LINING<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">NO EPOXY PAINT MANUFACTURER WILL EVER DECLARE IN WRITING HOW MUCH ACID PH VALUE THEIR PAINT CAN ENDURE.&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">If you ask them bluntly , they will stone wall you.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Do not load any cargoes in epoxy tanks which are not allowed by the paint manufacturer of your tank specific paint. &nbsp;Epoxy tanks can carry all types of cargoes from 4.5 to 14 pH.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: x-large;\"><br />\n</span></span></span></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: x-large;\">This means it cannot handle acids-- unless it is Siloxirane&nbsp;</span></span></span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow;\">.</span> Has limited resistance to Aromatics, Alcohols and Esters.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Pure epoxy paints are un-suitable for really corrosive liquids. All epoxy manufacturers specify that no aggressive cargo ( Ketones , Alcohols, Nitrites, Esters etc) should be loaded in the first 3 months . The next cargo after a previous aggressive cargo should be a fully approved non-aggressive cargo without any remark in the cargo resistant list.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; tab-stops: 10.2pt 94.95pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; tab-stops: 10.2pt 94.95pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">After carriage of \u201c<i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\">aggressive <b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\">water soluble</b> cargoes</i>\u201d, no steam, ballast water, wash water, slops or aqueous cargoes must come into contact with&nbsp; the epoxy coating before its original coating condition is <b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\">restored by ventilation</i></b>.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; tab-stops: 10.2pt 94.95pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; tab-stops: 10.2pt 94.95pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">When using Verveys guide pl remember \u2013it has not been made for smooth SS without internal framing\u2014and you will notice that no provision is made to remove aBsorbed chemical by venting. Indiscriminate jet impingement on unrecovered coating causes blisters and coating breakdown.. When an organic coating which is saturated with a water soluble solvent like Methanol or Ethanol is washed with water, severe blistering of the epoxy coating is sure to happen.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; tab-stops: 10.2pt 94.95pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; tab-stops: 10.2pt 94.95pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">More dangerous\u2014retained absorbed cargo in the epoxy coating film may cause a chemical reaction, and produce products, which cause total breakdown of the tank lining.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">l<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Cargoes such as Methanol and Benzene and Diethylene glycol are absorbed into the coating film to a higher degree than other chemicals .<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Remember the list of chemicals shown in the COF on a full epoxy coated ship is not the same as the resistance list of the paint manufacturer. Sometimes it is possible on a old ship to have three types of epoxies (Choguku/ Sigma --- pure/ phenolic/ isocyanate/ modified ) applied in different drydocks during her life time. When loading in epoxy tanks it is most necessary to see previous cargoes and check for footnotes in paint manufacturers list as to restrictions for next cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Epoxy paint is organic. It is a three dimensional \u201ccross linked array\u201d of chemical bonds between resin molecules. Amine cured epoxy is used on chemical tankers. Polyamine cured epoxy having no resistance to Aromatics is used on oil tankers usually.<b> The DFT </b>of an epoxy coating is usually specified to be between about 270 microns in a 3-coat system\u2014in unavoidable overlap areas and in unavoidable stripe coat areas it may be around 480 microns. These thick DFT areas&nbsp; are the vulnerable spots which take longer time to restore and remains soft . Doubling the DFT means desorbsion /drying times are four times longer.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">The paint is applied on a &nbsp;grit blasted to SA 2.5 surface. &nbsp;If the coating is too thick it will fall off when softened and pores opened by solvent cargoes like methanol, benzene and methyl acetate.&nbsp; High DFT causes longer time to cure after an aggressive cargo and can cause alligoration ( formation of cracks ). High film thickness requires longer ventilation than a low film thickness to get rid of entrapped solvent / cargo.<b> </b><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Sunlight can discolor the epoxy surface due to UV rays of the sun, but it should not affect the protective properties of the paint.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Cargoes tend to be aBsorbed like a sponge rather than aDsorbed. &nbsp;It reacts with water/ solvent mixtures which penetrate coating. So if ethanol is discharged the coating must not be allowed to get wet prior to venting. Unlike zinc silicate epoxy is usually touched up at sea ( on a degreased metal surface ) provided the curing time is sufficient. Phenolic and isocyanate epoxies are better than normal epoxy. Never recoat an epoxy coat on top of an old coat for the risk of poor bonding is too great. Degreasing must be done.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Aromatics like Benzene softens and swells epoxy. Do finger nail test prior tankwashing after aromatics, alcohols, esters and high FFA animal and veg oils. If your finger nail is not long enough use HB, 2B,4B, 6B pencils&nbsp; on breaking stress. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Enter tanks with soft soled shoes.&nbsp; If you make the mistake of speeding up recovery by application of heat from within the tank\u2014the top skin of coating will harder first thus trapping the solvent underneath. This solvent has to breakthrough and will bust the coating with flaking as a result. Recovery must be done by venting with application of heat from the other side, to increase VP and induce faster evaporation. &nbsp;I remember one of my past companies getting a horrendous claim of a couple of million dollars for loading Styrene Monomer in an epoxy tank after Benzene without extracting the aBsorbed Benzene by venting . One % absorbed previous cargo could cause a concentration of 10 ppm in the next cargo if completely dissolved. aBsorbsion always takes at a faster rate than release due to hydrostatic pressure or force feeding of sponge. Permeation is generally facilitated by increasing pigment content ( reduces when paint gloss reduces ). Absorbsion reaches equilibrium level in a few days and then remain constant.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">A 1000 cum tank AFTER 20 hours of ventilation can still contain 12 litres of methanol which can be released into the next cargo causing contamination and rejection of entire parcel. While a stainless steel tank or zinc tank after methanol discharge is ready for next cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp5\" style=\"line-height: normal; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">The best way to restore epoxy coating is&nbsp; with an air temperature of&nbsp; about 30C-- dry air with a relative humidity below 45%.&nbsp; At&nbsp; 15 C it takes more than&nbsp; 3 times the time..&nbsp; Paradoxically too high ventilation temperature does not speed up the restoring process and the epoxy film will remain soft even after the absorbed cargo is ventilated out of the coating<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">When an organic coating saturated with a water soluble sovent like Methanol or Ethanol is washed with water jets, severe blistering of paint takes place. Remember long term ventilation of empty tank at 30 deg C is required before water is introduced in the tank. Ventilate with dehumidified air for fast results. This is the reason why epoxy coated chemical tankers must have dehumidifier and heater inherent with the fixed blower. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Retained (aBsorbed ) cargoes which are water mixible or water reactive should NOT be removed by steaming or water jets . They also should not be followed by aqueous cargoes or ballast. Such a consideration is not there for Zinc Silicate which aDsorbs cargo ( aDsorbsion is a surface phenomenon). Empty epoxy cargo tanks which are not ventilated can sometimes be dangerous wrt explosion or toxicity. Entering such an ex Benzene tank is a sure way to invite cancer.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Adhesion of paint is tested by glued on tablets which are pulled off with a means of recording the force. Don\u2019t allow butterworth portable machines to bang during rolling.&nbsp; Epoxy coating should never be heated more than 80 degrees C during tankcleaning. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Methanol steaming is never done in epoxy tanks. No pure steaming must be done when the coating is soft. Solvent cargoes like Methanol ( moisture &lt;0.1% or 1000 ppm ) when mixed with water form aggressive acidic mixtures . Esters, Acetates, Chlorinated/ Brominated compounds, Pthalates will react with moisture to form acidic compounds ( moisture &lt;0.02% or 200 ppm ). <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">When oils and fats are contaminated with water they become more aggressive than their acid value alone would indicate. For this reason moisture content should not exceed 0.25%.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">It is better to do prompt and constant touch up when curing time is available , than to leave the damaged spots without touch up. Usually curing at 20C takes 10 days while at 30 deg C it takes 7 days. Spot portable grit blasters which do not allow grit to fly around are available in the market. Disc grinding causes poor adherence and paint will fall off contaminating cargo. While airless spot spraying remove adjacent cold ballast from adjacent tank and wrap steam coils in vicinity with old wire hoses. Stripe coating is applied on edges, welds and difficult to spray on areas.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Resistant to</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">: Normal epoxy has good resistance to Alkalies , veg oils and Luboil. Vegetable oils , animal oils and fats may be carried in epoxy tanks irrespective of acid value. For animal/ veg oils with a free fatty acid content content &gt;50% the temp of 50c must NOT be exceeded. Epoxy has good chemical solvent and water resistance. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Not resistant to:</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"> ( only for reference , for application CONSULT YOUR PAINT RESISTANCE TABLES INCLUDING EXCEPTIONS WRT WATER CONTENT ) all acids of pH less than 4.5 , Benzene, Toluene, Ethanol, Methanol, Esters, Ketones,&nbsp; Calcium Hypochlorite, HMD, Phosphoric acid , Nonyl Phenol, Sodium Hypochlorite soln &lt;15% , Sulphuric acid, 28% or less aqueous Ammonia, Chloro Toluene, Cyclo Hexylamine, Di Ethylamine, Diphenyl Ether, Di n Propylamine, Dodecyl Alchohol, Ethanolamine, Ferric Chloride soln, Furfural, Maleic Anhydride, Nonyl Phenol, Potassium Hydroxide soln, Sodium Hydrosulphide soln &lt; 45% , Sod Hydroxide soln, Tall oil, Undecyl Alcohol, Vinyl toluene,&nbsp; Xylenol, Acetone, Amyl alcohol, Alkaline Glycol Monoalkyl Ether, Bsolve, Di Ethyl Sulphate, Di isobutyl Ketone, Ethyl Acetate, Ethyl Acrylate, Ethylene Diamine, Ethyl Hexyl Acrylate, Isobutyl Acetate, Polyethylene Polyamine, Isobutyl mix, Brake fluid, Polythelene Polyamine, Propionic acid, Triethylene Tetramine, Propelene Glycol, Methyl Ether Acetate, Vinyl Acetate etc etc .<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Epoxy and modified epoxy are resistant to very few amines ( Zinc is better only if theses Amines are water free ) . Steaming of tanks for prolonged periods can cause damage. The thing to make sure is that the steel temp does not exceed 50 deg C. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">If the difference between cargo temp and empty tank temp is &gt;55 deg C it is recommended that preheating of tanks is done prior loading to prevent thermal shock. In case of Aliphatic petroleum products example: Crude oil, Waxes, Bitumens, a max carriage temp of 70 deg C may be accepted <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">The hardener and resin mix has a low pot life. Coating chalks and yellows on ageing . Acetic acid can be used to refresh and to remove lead from Gasoline trapped within. Some companies suggest recirc of Metalbrite / &nbsp;Phosphoric acid . REMEMBER any acid of less pH than 4.5 will damage the epoxy coating . You have to use the pH value paper. Remember DILUTING STRONG ACIDS BY A FACTOR OF TEN INCREASES pH VALUE BY A MEASLY ONE. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Paint manufacturers indicate suitability based on max transport temperature. They usually mention higher heating limits for a limited number of days. Example: can be heated to 75 deg C for 10 days. Consult paint manufacturers resistance suitability notes for such information. A paint manufacturers resistance list footnote might say\u2014<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Tank must be left dry prior loading.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">&nbsp;OR<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Next cargo must be a hot cargo of Lubes / Mineral/ Veg / Animal oil for min 5 days at 50 deg C or 43 days at 60 deg C. OR<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Non aggressive , non aqueous cargoes must be carried for 30 days.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Water mixible cargoes must be carried in perfectly dry tanks and water must be excluded during carriage. &nbsp;Prior tankcleaning ,vent the tank etc etc.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">If you ballast epoxy cargo tank the ballast water surface must be chased down using tank cleaning machines during the deballasting process lest you get a stained /discoloured coating. During long voyages change the ballast every 10 days. Epoxy is however the best for salt water ballast followed by Zinc and last stainless steel.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Epoxy does not absorb oils, they absorb only solvents. During wall wash test the \u201ctest Methanol\u201d &nbsp;swells the coating and extracts the residues. Some cargoes get chemically bonded to the coating by molecular forces. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp4\" style=\"line-height: normal; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Liquid is&nbsp; absorbed by the binder phase of the coating through the diffusion process till it is saturated.. Desorbsion also takes place by the diffusion process..<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">The following cargoes swells epoxy and MUST be ventilated prior washing with jets.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Acetate<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Acetone<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Acrylonitrile<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Adiponitrile<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Butyl acetate<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Cyclohexane<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">EDC<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Ekta solve DP<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Ekta solve EB<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Ekta solve EE<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Ektapro EEP<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Ethyl acetate<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">IPA<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Isopropyl acetate<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">MEK<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Methanol<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Methyl acetate<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Styrene monomer<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Vinyl acetate monomer<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">In general cargoes having small molecular structures are able to penetrate organic coatings to a greater extent than those cargoes with larger molecules. So Methanol is a very penetrative cargo. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Since epoxy is like a sponge \u2013to lessen absorbsion of cargo into the paint layer, it is better to carry cargo ( in shipowners interests ) at the lowest possible practical temperature.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Wall wash surveyors are quite particular about odour in an epoxy tank when sensitive odour absorbing cargoes such as edible oils, potable Ethanol, MEG FG etc are to be carried. &nbsp;A strong smelling cargo like Styrene Monomer absorbed into coating can still give potent odour and contaminate a sensitive heated vegetable oil after 2 voyages. This is the reason why FOSFA has banned Styrene/ EDC as the LAST TWO cargoes in epoxy tanks. Heating increases the rate of desorbsion<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Two successive cargoes may require to be chemically compatible with each other.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">WARNING:--Epoxy paint is non toxic only after curing. Be aware of the curing time in case you need to spot touch up. The time versus temperature scale is always given in the paint tables.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">IT IS THE MASTERS DUTY TO ADVISE WHOM SO EVER IT MAY CONCERN ABOUT THE DANGERS OF DESORBED CARGO (FROM SPONGY EPOXY CONTAMINATING THE WHOLE SHIPMENT). &nbsp;&nbsp;WHEN THINGS GO WRONG ALL AND SUNDRY (WHO WERE AVERSE TO TIME LOSS DUE TO VENTILATION) &nbsp;NOW WILL WASH OFF THEIR HANDS LEAVING THE SHIPOWNER ALL ALONE WITH A HUGE FINANCIAL BURDEN AND LOSS OF IMAGE.<br style=\"mso-special-character: line-break;\" /> <br style=\"mso-special-character: line-break;\" /> <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">PHENOLIC EPOXIES</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"> <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Phenolic resins can handle strong solvent chemicals which epoxies and polyurethane coatings cannot . it has the highest resistance to chemicals.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Phenolic epoxies are better for low molecular weight Alcohols, Ketones , Aromatics like BTX. Esters (Acetates, Pthalates ) Chlorinated / Brominated materials that react with water to form acidic compounds. Water content greater than 200ppm or 0.02% must be avoided. When Methanol and Vinyl acetate monomer is carried in Phenolic epoxy tanks a hot cure is required. Example: the paint resistance tables might talk about carrying heated LO , Veg oil or animal oil at 60 deg C for 5 days. Phenolic resins are expensive . They can load solvents which cant be loaded in epoxy and polyurethane.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; tab-stops: 10.2pt 94.95pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-left: 0in; tab-stops: 10.2pt 94.95pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">After carrying &nbsp;Ketones,&nbsp; Ethers and Esters the tank should be well ventilated to remove all traces of the previous cargo prior to cleaning\u2014and the next cargo should not be diluted aqueous solutions like latex or fertilizer solutions.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-top: 8.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: -34.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The absorbsion of epoxy is faster than desorbsion due to hydrostatic pressure of cargo. Epoxy acts like a sponge, especially if the pigmentation is good. The organic molecules of the epoxy coat is permeated by the cargo of low molecular structure causing softening.&nbsp; Modified epoxies are most exposed to this problem\u2014as they are ABLE to carry such products<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">POLYURETHANE: <o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Normal epoxy has limited time exposure to high acid animal and vegetable oils. &nbsp;But Polyurethane can stand acid conditions from free Fatty acids.&nbsp; But it is not as good as normal epoxy for Caustics. &nbsp;Also it can take the Ketones and Alcohol solvents epoxy cannot handle. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Another good thing is that the polyurethane lining has a smooth finish , it wont have too much clingage and so it is easy to clean. Urethane epoxies do not absorb and hold much solvents\u2014--but Amine epoxies and Phenolic epoxies hold nearly double the content. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Can be provided as one or two pack product. One pack depends on atmosphereic moisture to produce polymerisation. Two pack is more common.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Camrex camcote MX </span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">is resistant to Ethanol and Methanol.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">RUBBER:</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"> <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Rubber is used for highly corrosive cargoes which cannot be handled by Epoxy, Phenolic epoxy, Polyurethane and even stainless steel.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Rubber is suitable for Phosphoric acid. But not for Nitric acid and Sulphuric acid. It is used primarily for Hydrochloric acid and waste acids. The rubber lining is usually 6mm thick and can be of the Neoprene, Chloroprene, Nitryl and Butyl variety. There can be no perforation in the coating. Rubber coating is expensive. And must be done at drydock in ideal conditions ( temperature and humidity controlled ) on ideal surface, gritblasted , dust free ( vacuumed ) and degreased.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Rubber is not suitable for Nitric and Sulphuric acids as they oxidize rubber. Rubber is not suitable for vegetable oils , animal oils or solvents<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"tab-stops: 10.2pt; text-align: justify;\"><b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">POLYESTER</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"> <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"tab-stops: 10.2pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\">Has better resistance to acids than epoxy or polyurethane but has poor resistance to solvents and alkalies. So used in organic acid trade \u2013limited use.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"tab-stops: 10.2pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"tab-stops: 10.2pt; text-align: justify;\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQhZQCdsrgI/AAAAAAAAB9Y/eJxnhloKuNo/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQhZQCdsrgI/AAAAAAAAB9Y/eJxnhloKuNo/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" /></a></div><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"tab-stops: 10.2pt; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL ( 28 YEARS IN COMMAND )</span></div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "38", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/2867893707292367609/comments"}}, {"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "4265676898448685320", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2010-06-01T19:28:00+05:30", "updated": "2011-09-13T11:03:43+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxMzE1ODkyMDIzMDE1Cm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2010/06/basics-for-chemical-tankerman-capt-ajit.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/4265676898448685320", "title": "BASICS FOR THE CHEMICAL TANKERMAN  --  CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: left;\" trbidi=\"on\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Arial;
